target=\"_blank\" data-popup\n        rel=\"nofollow\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-linkedin\">\n            \n                2\n            \n        </span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-linkedin\">LINKEDIN</span></a><span\n            class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-comments\"\n            data-share-method=\"comments\"\n            data-uotrack=\"InlineShareCommentsBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-comments\">\n                \n                    22\n                \n            </span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-comments\">COMMENT</span></span><span\n        class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-email\"\n        data-share-method=\"email\"\n        data-uotrack=\"InlineShareEmailBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-email\"></span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-email\">EMAIL</span></span><span\n         class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-more\"\n         data-share-method=\"facebook\"\n         data-uotrack=\"InlineShareMoreBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-more\"></span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-more\">MORE</span></span></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>A growing brush fire in South Florida destroyed destroyed buildings and forced thousands of people from their homes as emergency crews from across the state scrambled Saturday to beat back the blaze.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Rain fell Saturday, offering some respite to the 240 firefighters fighting a blaze in Collier County near Naples, .But officials warned residents not to read too much into the showers.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cIt\u2019s great that we got the rain,\u201d Florida Gov. Rick Scott said at a briefing. \u201cBut it didn\u2019t stop the fire.\u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div class=\"partner-placement partner-spike\"></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>As of late Saturday afternoon, the blaze is at 5,500 acres in Collier County, with 20% containment, according to Scott. The blaze destroyed <a href=\"/story/news/local/2017/04/22/picking-up-remains-residents-golden-gate-estates-come-homes-cars-destroyed-brush-fire/100782440/\">nine homes, as well as some cars</a>, in the past day, officials said.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>One person has been reported injured. Ngala wildlife refuge CEO Donovan Smith suffered second-degree burns Friday as he fought off flames closing in on a rhinoceros named Walter, Smith posted on his Facebook page Friday. Walter survived. Smith was taken to a Tampa hospital for treatment.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div class=\"partner-outstream\"></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Local government first ordered mandatory evacuations on Thursday as the then-400-acre fire threatened a large residential part of Naples. By the next day it had grown to more than 10\u00a0times the size.\u00a0Officials confirmed that residents in 7,000 homes have been ordered to evacuate, although\u00a0some people have chosen not to leave.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>More than 100 Florida Forest Service crews are on the ground battling the blaze along with more than 300 contractors, plus law enforcement. On Friday, Scott deployed National Guard resources to assist, along with a stern warning to residents.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"These wildfires are dangerous and if you're within the evacuation area, do not stay in your home,\" he said Friday. \"Be sure to follow the evacuation orders from local officials.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Scott, after meeting with emergency officials Saturday, promised to stand by those affected and urged people to follow evacuation orders.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"Let's be clear, these fires are dangerous. They're extremely dangerous so we need to be very cautious,\" he said. \"The direction of the fire can change in a moment's notice and the fire can move very very very rapidly.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Scott\u00a0lauded President Trump's administration, which he said was \"very responsive\" to the fire. The federal government will help reimburse Florida for the costs associated with fighting the fire. Scott clarified he hasn't talked to the president about the matter. The state couldn't provide an estimate as to how much the firefighting effort will cost.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P5aICDpJ1FA\" class=\"story-asset gallery-asset\"><div cxenseparse_start --><p>Officials said Saturday they had hoped to contain the fire overnight, but to no avail. Kingman\u00a0Shuldt, a fire chief with Greater Naples Fire agency, said the fire is pressing westward. There's worry if the fire jumps a popular thoroughfare, it could threaten more densely populated areas.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Schuldt said ground in the area is very dry, describing it as \"double dead.\" He said crews are preparing for another firefight on Saturday.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"It's a very dangerous task out there,\" he said. \"Very very dangerous.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>A light rain started to fall Saturday afternoon and crews said they had made progress in containing the fire. <a href=\"/story/news/local/2017/04/22/saturday-update-golden-gate-estates-brush-fires-collier-county-30th-avenue-fire/100781188/\">Bulldozers had cleared</a> debris said to be fueling the blaze.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Officials offered no time frame as to when residents evacuated from their homes will be able to return home. That, they said, depends on the progress\u00a0made\u00a0fighting the fire.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Dan Summers, Collier County's director of emergency services, said as many as 10 airplanes would be doing water drops\u00a0in the area on Saturday.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>On Friday, the National Guard was deploying Blackhawk helicopters to help tame the 100-foot flames.\u00a0About 100 deputies went through neighborhoods and door to door to try to evacuate residents.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Officials on Saturday didn't offer a reason for how the fire started, saying the cause of the blaze is under investigation.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The Sunshine State has seen a steep increase in wildfires in 2017.\u00a0Earlier this month, Scott issued a state of emergency, adding\u00a0there are more than 100 active wildfires across the state threatening about 20,000 acres of land. In the first three months of 2017, wildfires burned 250% more land in Florida than they had in the same time frame the year before.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Scott said the state also continues to battle other fires outside of Naples, including a more than 600-acre fire in Polk County, which has prompted mandatory evacuations in the central part of the state. A more than 400-acre fire in Lee County, just north of Naples,\u00a0has already damaged or destroyed 13 homes and caused the mandatory evacuations of more than 2,000 homes. Later on Saturday, the governor will visit the damage in Lee County.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><em>Follow Sean Rossman on Twitter: <a href=\"https://twitter.com/SeanRossman\">@SeanRossman</a></em></p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P5aICDoYrf0\" class=\"story-asset inline-share-tools-asset\"><div (Photo: Ryan Mills/Naples Daily News)\n\nA growing brush fire in South Florida destroyed destroyed buildings and forced thousands of people from their homes as emergency crews from across the state scrambled Saturday to beat back the blaze.\n\nRain fell Saturday, offering some respite to the 240 firefighters fighting a blaze in Collier County near Naples, .But officials warned residents not to read too much into the showers.\n\n\u201cIt\u2019s great that we got the rain,\u201d Florida Gov. Rick Scott said at a briefing. \u201cBut it didn\u2019t stop the fire.\u201d\n\nAs of late Saturday afternoon, the blaze is at 5,500 acres in Collier County, with 20% containment, according to Scott. The blaze destroyed nine homes, as well as some cars, in the past day, officials said.\n\nOne person has been reported injured. Ngala wildlife refuge CEO Donovan Smith suffered second-degree burns Friday as he fought off flames closing in on a rhinoceros named Walter, Smith posted on his Facebook page Friday. Walter survived. Smith was taken to a Tampa hospital for treatment.\n\nLocal government first ordered mandatory evacuations on Thursday as the then-400-acre fire threatened a large residential part of Naples. By the next day it had grown to more than 10 times the size. Officials confirmed that residents in 7,000 homes have been ordered to evacuate, although some people have chosen not to leave.\n\nMore than 100 Florida Forest Service crews are on the ground battling the blaze along with more than 300 contractors, plus law enforcement. On Friday, Scott deployed National Guard resources to assist, along with a stern warning to residents.\n\n\"These wildfires are dangerous and if you're within the evacuation area, do not stay in your home,\" he said Friday. \"Be sure to follow the evacuation orders from local officials.\"\n\nScott, after meeting with emergency officials Saturday, promised to stand by those affected and urged people to follow evacuation orders.\n\n\"Let's be clear, these fires are dangerous. They're extremely dangerous so we need to be very cautious,\" he said. \"The direction of the fire can change in a moment's notice and the fire can move very very very rapidly.\"\n\nScott lauded President Trump's administration, which he said was \"very responsive\" to the fire. The federal government will help reimburse Florida for the costs associated with fighting the fire. Scott clarified he hasn't talked to the president about the matter. The state couldn't provide an estimate as to how much the firefighting effort will cost.\n\nOfficials said Saturday they had hoped to contain the fire overnight, but to no avail. Kingman Shuldt, a fire chief with Greater Naples Fire agency, said the fire is pressing westward. There's worry if the fire jumps a popular thoroughfare, it could threaten more densely populated areas.\n\nSchuldt said ground in the area is very dry, describing it as \"double dead.\" He said crews are preparing for another firefight on Saturday.\n\n\"It's a very dangerous task out there,\" he said. \"Very very dangerous.\"\n\nA light rain started to fall Saturday afternoon and crews said they had made progress in containing the fire. Bulldozers had cleared debris said to be fueling the blaze.\n\nOfficials offered no time frame as to when residents evacuated from their homes will be able to return home. That, they said, depends on the progress made fighting the fire.\n\nDan Summers, Collier County's director of emergency services, said as many as 10 airplanes would be doing water drops in the area on Saturday.\n\nOn Friday, the National Guard was deploying Blackhawk helicopters to help tame the 100-foot flames. About 100 deputies went through neighborhoods and door to door to try to evacuate residents.\n\nOfficials on Saturday didn't offer a reason for how the fire started, saying the cause of the blaze is under investigation.\n\nThe Sunshine State has seen a steep increase in wildfires in 2017. Earlier this month, Scott issued a state of emergency, adding there are more than 100 active wildfires across the state threatening about 20,000 acres of land. In the first three months of 2017, wildfires burned 250% more land in Florida than they had in the same time frame the year before.\n\nScott said the state also continues to battle other fires outside of Naples, including a more than 600-acre fire in Polk County, which has prompted mandatory evacuations in the central part of the state. A more than 400-acre fire in Lee County, just north of Naples, has already damaged or destroyed 13 homes and caused the mandatory evacuations of more than 2,000 homes. Later on Saturday, the governor will visit the damage in Lee County.\n\nFollow Sean Rossman on Twitter: @SeanRossman\n\nRead or Share this story: http://usat.ly/2p6ZJ2B", "images":
